 On October 18, 1962, the Central Intelligence Agency released a ""Joint Evaluation of the Soviet Mission Threat in Cuba" based on intelligence obtained as of 9m. that day .
 The evaluation was codenamed Iron Bark because it drew upon intelligence material provided by the Central Intelligence Agency's important Soviet source, Colonel Oleg Penkovsky .
 It was based on photo interpretation of U-2 photography made on October 14, and two on October 15 and two of six missions on October 17 . The analysis was made based on "very preliminary and incomplete readout"
 These mobile missiles had to be considered operational and could be launched within 18 hours after the decision to launch was made . Mobile missiles could launch within the next 18 hours of a launch decision .
 These sites were probably intended for 2200nm intermediate-range ballistic missiles and could be operational by December 1962 . The sites were likely to be operational in December 1962.
 All missiles were manned by Soviet personnel and were under Soviet control . The missiles were launched in the 1980s and 1991 .
 The expected warheads for these missiles would weigh 3,000 pounds and have yield in the low megaton range . The warheads would be expected to weigh around 3,500 pounds .
 The significance of these developments was that the Soviet Union ""intends to develop Cuba into a prime strategic base, rather than as a token show of force", according to the evaluation .
 The mixed force of 1020-and 2200nm missiles posed a common threat to the U.S. and a large portion of Latin America . The mix of missiles was created in the 1980s .

 Last month I stated publicly that the U.S. would consider the presence of ground-to-ground missiles in Cuba as an offensive threat . You will recall that last month .
 The foregoing has created a highly critical situation which must be met promptly and fearlessly . The situation is a 'highly critical situation' for the country .

 Ambassador Bruce will also be prepared to explain to you the evidence on which we have based our conclusions . Ambassador Bruce is also prepared fully to explain the evidence that we have .
 I am also writing to Chairman Khrushchev to bring home to him how perilous is his present course of action, but expressing the hope that we can agree to resume the path of peaceful negotiation .
 I am quite clear in my mind that these missiles have got to be withdrawn, and you will see that I intend to state this publicly in my speech as well as telling Chairman Khrushchev this in my letter to him .
 The object of the quarantine, which will be put into effect immediately, is to prevent the Soviet Union from introducing additional missiles into Cuba and to lead to the elimination of the missiles that are already in place .

 A challenge at sea to the quarantine is unlikely, at least for a day or two . A challenge is unlikely to be made at sea at sea .
 Thereafter a challenge is likely if the Soviets believe that their political efforts are not succeeding and a heightening of the crisis is required . Thereafter, a challenge will likely be likely to be needed if the Soviet leadership is not succeeding .
 Retaliatory actions would follow if the incident itself failed to produce quick political results . The incident would be the first time the U.S. government has been involved in a political crisis .
 It would be aimed either at a U.S. ship elsewhere or at access to Berlin . We think the latter somewhat more likely .
 TASS statement suggests that the Soviets wish to retain full freedom of action while they consider their initial moves .
 There is some intelligence, dating from before the President's speech, indicating that the Soviets had decided to run any U.S. blockade which might be established .
 We think it likely that, at least for a day or two, they will avoid a challenge at sea while they observe the results of their political efforts to get the quarantine lifted . Nevertheless, we think it will likely be a challenge for them .
 If the USSR feels that these efforts are succeeding, the Soviets will probably continue to avoid challenges, lest an incident interrupt this favorable trend . If the Soviets feel successful, they will probably not be challenged again . The Soviet Union will continue to ignore challenges .
 If and when they decide to permit an incident of this sort, the Soviets would not allow the U.S. to board a vessel, since this would mean acceptance in principle of quarantine .
 Instead of attacking a ship carrying a nonmilitary cargo, the U.S. would probably be choosing a ship with a non-military cargo and allowing it to be attacked .
 It is possible that the Soviets, in deciding to test the quarantine, would accompany their probe ship with a submarine which would counterattack the United States vessel after the Soviet ship was struck .
 The Soviets would almost certainly think the U.S. would respond by tightening the blockade and launching a full-scale effort to seek out and destroy a Soviet submarine in the area of quarantine operations . We think this unlikely, however, because the United States would tighten the blockade .
 After an incident, the Soviets would probably allow a pause while they exploited this incident and observed its effects . The Soviets probably allowed a pause to observe the effects of the incident .
 Unless the U.S. showed signs of quickly yielding, however, they would then follow with some form of retaliation . The United States would then likely follow with a retaliatory response, says CNN.com.com .
 "We do not believe that this would take the form of major military action," says CNN.com . We do not think this would be the first major action against Syria .
 The Soviets would choose between an attack on a U.S. ship elsewhere or a move on the access routes to Berlin . The move was designed to remind the United States of the vulnerability of its position in Berlin .
 In most circumstances, they probably would regard a Berlin move as both more effective and easier to control . Berlin move is likely to be more effective than any other move .
 The USSR might use a submarine, however, to deliver through the quarantine some particularly critical item, to demonstrate its ability to frustrate U.S. efforts .

 The USSR's first objective in the present stage of the crisis is to retain the bases in Cuba . The USSR is seeking to retain control of Cuba's bases in the country .
 The immediate Soviet aim is to deter the United States from more drastic action . Thus the immediate Soviet attempt is to . deter the U.S. from more . drastic action. Thus the . immediate . Soviet aim was to deter . from more radical action .
 Their diplomatic moves and conduct at sea to date suggest that they fear further U.S. action may be imminent . They wish not to have their prestige further engaged if this should occur .
 The primary Soviet tactic will be to draw the United States into negotiations, meanwhile getting a standstill . The United States is getting stuck in negotiations with Russia .
 The Soviets calculate that, if this can be done, they will have laid heavy inhibitions upon further U.S. unilateral action . With the passage of time, the existing bases will become part of the status quo, the Soviets calculate .
 They prefer the lifting of the quarantine be made a precondition of negotiations, but they probably will not insist upon this . They prefer, of course, that lifting the quarantine is a pre-condition of negotiations .
 US-Soviet-Cuban talks are likely to take place in Cuba . They will probably propose or accept any of several forms of negotiation .
 At the present juncture the Soviets probably view a summit meeting as an appealing proposal to keep open the line of negotiation, especially if a stalemate in UN approaches which might free the United States to take military action .
 With a summit in prospect they would estimate the pressures for the U.S. to wait would be great . With the pressures on the United States to wait for the summit, they say .
 A summit therefore would buy the Soviets some additional time, offer a forum to make a reasonable case, confuse the issues, and raise the political costs of further U.S. action .
 At the same time, they would not want to be faced at the summit with an ultimatum or an unyielding United States position . If it resulted in further actions, further actions would redouble the humiliation to the USSR and Khrushchev personally . The U.S.
 U.S. summit offers more advantages than drawbacks, analysts say . On balance they probably feel that as long as the United States did not appear determined to take action, the summit offers advantages .
 Although the Soviets would like to minimize the risks at the present juncture, they find it very difficult to acquiesce in the United States quarantine . The U.S. government is quarantined the U.N. quarantine .

 There is one circumstance, however, in which a break in this Soviet position might occur, might occur .

 One-OCI analysis of two Soviet letters to the U.S. of 26 and 27 October . The letters were sent to the United States .
 The likeliest explanation of Soviet behavior in addressing two inconsistent letters to the President in such short succession is that they came to believe that the U.S. intended firm or radical action against the Cuban bases at a fairly early date .
 They sent a second letter containing a more specific proposal, but one involving substantial Soviet concessions, in an effort to generate pressures which would head off this U.S. action or, if this failed, to make it as costly as possible in political terms .
 The Soviets can, if they choose, repeat their Cuba-Turkey offer and complain that U.S. preconditions amount to an unacceptable ultimatum . But they probably now recognize that this may not deflect the United States from its insist-ence that the sites be immediately dismantled .
 The U.S. can alter tactics radically, going over to a threatening line in their statements and buttressing this with a deliberate maritime incident in the Caribbean and moves to globalize the crisis, e.g., some action against Berlin . Or they can alter .
 Their tactics to date, however, and their apparent belief that the United States is determined on further actions, argue strongly against this latter course . The U.S. has not responded to the situation in Syria .
 A third course would be to accept some of the conditions stated by the United States today and to continue the search for negotiations which would lay inhibitions on further unilateral moves .
 In return for a removal of weapons from Turkey, the Soviets have now offered substantial concessions . The move would raise doubts in that country and in NATO as a whole concerning the U.S. commitment .
 In the process, the Soviets have gone far to acknowledge the truth of the President's original charges . The Soviet Union has gone far further to admit the truth .
 They have made statements which must seriously undermine Castro's confidence in Soviet support, and even Soviet intentions . As another result, they have made . statements which have seriously undermined Castro's . confidence in . Soviet support .
 The next Soviet position may be less demanding than the Cuba-Turkey swap . Russia's position may not be as demanding as that of Turkey's .
 We think that they might limit their demands to a U.S. undertaking not to pursue Castro's overthrow, we think . The United States might limit its demands to an agreement not to overthrow Castro's regime .
 In return, they might agree to cease work on those sites which are not yet operational and to discuss means of ""rendering the weapons inoperable,"" and to move toward international inspection .

 The proposal, he noted, intentionally bypassed the United States Mission at the United Nations . The proposal is intentionally bypasses the U.S. mission at the UN .
 The intention was to make it appear to be a United Nations proposal, rather than one that originated in Washington . The intention is to make the proposal appear to have originated in the United States .
